                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-108025081133" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <div>
                          <p>
                           <span>
                           </span>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="The Best 7 Strength Exercises You're Not Doing" height="400" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w620/243ee20bbe2391e9e781171ee1bd0d0fe85ebb77.jpg" title="The 7 Best Strength Exercises You're Not Doing" width="620"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (Photo:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.pond5.com/photo/33343039/dumbbells.html" target="_blank">
                             Pond5
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <p>
                          Every exercise in your strength program has a purpose  to help you build strength and muscle,burn fat, and improve your fitness. While theres a time and a place for nearly any exercise under the right circumstance,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/fitness/high-intensity-hiit-workout/?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises" target="_blank">
                           some movements
                          </a>
                          are simply more effective than others. And it should be no surprise that the ones that build a foundation for skills that youll use in real life will be the most beneficial for improving your fitness and quality of life.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           <strong>
                            Related:
                           </strong>
                           <em>
                            <strong>
                             <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/fitness/common-workout-setbacks/?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises" target="_blank">
                              <span>
                               10 Ways Youre Sabotaging Your Workout
                              </span>
                             </a>
                            </strong>
                           </em>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          So how does a lifter ensure theyre making all the right moves?If youve plateauedor just arent seeing the results youre banking on, its time to get
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/fitness/how-to-build-muscle-fast-pick-weights/?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises" target="_blank">
                           back to basics
                          </a>
                          with these seven moves. From increased strength, better core stability, greaterathleticism, and improved overall health, these key exercises need to find their way into your routine.
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="Goblet Squat" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/4a5f6ad7101f4ffd4c5e0f0866e8341118643a9e.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MeIiIdhvXT4" target="_blank">
                             Scott Herman Fitness
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <h3>
                          <strong>
                           1. Goblet Squat
                          </strong>
                         </h3>
                         <p>
                          Squats are an exercise many people struggle to perform safely and effectively. Luckily,the goblet squatis a great progression from a bodyweight squat before squatting with a bar. Because the load is held in front, the core works double-time to keep you tall, while your legs work to control your movement down and stand back up.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           <strong>
                            <strong>
                             Related:
                            </strong>
                            <em>
                             <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/fitness/mental-trick-maintain-strength/?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises" target="_blank">
                              <span>
                               The 5-Second Mental Trick That Could Help You Maintain Strength
                              </span>
                             </a>
                            </em>
                           </strong>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Hold a dumbbell with both hands underneath the bell at chest level, and set your feet shoulder-width apart with your toes pointing slightly outwards (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). Push your butt back like youre sitting in a chair and descend until your elbows reach the inside of your knees. (
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). Keeping your heels flat, pressing jnto the floor, pause at the bottom of the squat, and return to a full standing position. If your heels rise push your hips further back and work on partial ranges of motion until mobility and form improve (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ). Repeat for four sets of 8-10 reps.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           <strong>
                            <strong>
                             Related:
                            </strong>
                            <em>
                             <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/recipes/protein-smoothie-recipes/?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises" target="_blank">
                              <span>
                               7 Delicious Protein Smoothie Recipes
                              </span>
                             </a>
                            </em>
                           </strong>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="Pallof Press" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/7bd83a76cdc27e2970d546081bc1f0f1b97d9510.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bzE553my1o8&amp;feature=youtu.be" target="_blank">
                             Tony Gentilcore
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <h3>
                          <strong>
                           2. Pallof Press
                          </strong>
                         </h3>
                         <p>
                          The Pallof press is one of those movements that looks confusing, but is actually incredibly simple and beneficial, says Mike Campbell, personal trainer and owner ofUnleash Your Alpha. While you may not be hoisting heavy weight, the real challenge lies in
                          <em>
                           resisting
                          </em>
                          movement  in this case, rotation. That makes this an anti-rotation movement, forcing you to engage through your entire core: obliques, abs, lower back, glutes and more. According to Campbell, the Paloff press will build great usable strength while adding athletic definition through the mid-section (in coordination with a sound diet).
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           <strong>
                            Related:
                            <em>
                             <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/fitness/beginner-crossfit-workouts/?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises" target="_blank">
                              <span>
                               5 Beginner-Friendly CrossFit Workouts
                              </span>
                             </a>
                            </em>
                           </strong>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Stand perpendicular to a cable column with the columns arm set around shoulder height. Grab the handle with both hands and pull it in to the chest, maintaining tension on the cable. Feet should be shoulder-width apart, and the feet, knees, hips and shoulders all remain square and facing straight ahead throughout movement (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). Holding the chest high, squeeze through the stomach and press the handle away from the body, extending the arms straight while resisting any twisting or rotation (
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). Its at this point the resistance will be highest. Continue to engage your core, and ensure you remain square and straight and resist the rotational force. Bring arms back in to the chest and repeat for three sets of 10 reps per side (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ).
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://cdn3.dailyburn.com/life/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/One-Arm-Dumbbell-Row.gif" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="One Arm Dumbbell Row" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/c663f42acc7cfc46fcec7daca4e6bede83b7a995.gif" height="226" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          </a>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ovTHP1MZbZI" target="_blank">
                             infosport
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <h3>
                          <strong>
                           3. Dumbbell Row
                          </strong>
                         </h3>
                         <p>
                          Most of us spend more time training the mirror muscles on the front of the body, and neglect what we cant see, according to Campbell. But developing a strong back is key to balance things out, improve posture andavoid injury. The dumbbell row can help achieve all that, in addition building strong arms and a strong core. The main muscles being used are the lats, traps and rhomboids, which reinforce good posture by pulling your shoulders back and aiding the core in stabilizing your spine.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Grab a dumbbell (20 pounds is plenty for most to start) and find a bench. Start with your left hand on the bench with left arm extended, while your right arm holds the dumbbell and right foot is on the ground (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). Retract your shoulders, brace your abs, and pull the weight up on the side of your body until the elbow passes the side of the body (
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). Lower under control and repeat for three sets of 6-8 reps on each side (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ).
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="Push Up" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/0538bd62f3d9280916e85bfcdb0426558175e612.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://dailyburn.com/life/fitness/perfect-push-up-workout-video/" target="_blank">
                             DailyBurn
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <h3>
                          <strong>
                           4. Push-Up
                          </strong>
                         </h3>
                         <p>
                          Thepush-upmight appear basic, but its one of the best exercises you can do. The functional movement is great for training the upper-body pushing muscles  the anterior deltoids, triceps and chest. It also requires you to engage your core and allows full range of motion in your shoulder blades, unlike the bench press.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Start on your knees facing the floor with your hands at shoulder-width, planted directly under the shoulders. Assume a plank position by straightening your legs, supporting your weight with hands and feet (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). Squeeze your backside to keep your trunk engaged and lower your body slowly to the ground. The elbows should be slightly tucked  like arrows, rather than flared like the letter T (
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). Descend until your chest is just above the ground and return to the starting position by fully extending your arms, and repeat (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ). Note: If you cant do five push-ups with good form, elevate your hands on a bench or chair to begin building up your strength. If push-ups are easy,try elevating your feeton a chair on adding a weight vest. Make sure youre able to perform three sets of 12 push-ups with your bodyweight before adding a vest or elevating your feet.
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="Split Squat" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/a42dad071727e39d308f306e4d4f01eec462a44a.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=z0NUTXY1vF0" target="_blank">
                             Howcast Sports Fitness
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <h3>
                          <strong>
                           5. Split Squat
                          </strong>
                         </h3>
                         <p>
                          Traditional squats are great, but its important to incorporate single-leg movements to develop athleticism andminimize training imbalances. The split squat, a stationary lunge, does just that. The split stance requires you to balance with a narrow base of support, firing up stabilizing muscles of the hip and trunk while training your quads, glutes and hamstrings to perform the movement. In addition to buildinglower-body strength, the single-leg nature of the exercise helps improve balance and increase flexibility and stability in the hips.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Stand with feet shoulder-width apart. Next, take a step forward with your right foot, and a large step backwards with your left foot  this is your starting position (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). Keep the front heel flat and descend into a lunge, bringing your back knee towards the floor. Stop just short of the knee touching the ground on the back leg with the front heel still flat on the ground (
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). Pause for one second and return to standing. Perform 6-8 reps on your right leg, then 6-8 reps on your left leg, and repeat for three sets (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ).
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="Lateral Squat" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/8d997ede9fb5f45fdbc1e29b8dc9a14a2d0832f1.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.coreperformance.com/knowledge/movements/lateral-squat.html" target="_blank">
                             Core Performance
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           6. Lateral Squat
                          </strong>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The lateral squat combines two movements: a lateral lunge and a squat. The difference? The lateral squat is stationary. It requires you to move side-to-side, providing a great stretch on the groin and inner thighs while training the hips, thighs and trunk to work together. Life isnt strictly moving forwards and backwards. Its best that your training isnt either.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Stand tall with your feet wider than shoulder-width apart, heels flat on the ground and toes pointed forward. Initiate the movement by pushing your hips backwards, bending your left leg, and leaning to your left with your right foot angled out slightly (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). The left knee should be bent, left heel flat on the floor, and right leg extended with your weight over the left side of your body (
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). This is one rep. Return to a standing position and descend doing the same movement on your right side to even things out (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ). Perform six reps per leg for three sets.
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <img alt="Glute Bridge" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/diminuendo/1.0/original/27addc7a070f8297a75bd3765f24d4c73a499278.gif" height="225" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="400"/>
                          <p>
                           <em>
                            (GIF:
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:9e63235a-15a3-3143-909d-0962e87179fc;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SEdqd1n0cvg" target="_blank">
                             Scott Herman Fitness
                            </a>
                            )
                           </em>
                          </p>
                         </div>
                         <h3>
                          7
                          <strong>
                           . Hip Extension (Glute Bridges/Hip Thrusts)
                          </strong>
                         </h3>
                         <p>
                          One of the most important muscle groups for any trainee  athlete, weekend warrior, or newbie  is the glutes. Yet they are often neglected and underutilized from sitting for long periods each day. According to Campbell, When we attempt movements from running to squatting without optimal hip movement we risk injury to our hips, knees and ankles. Getting glutes that not only switch on when they should but are strong is crucial, and thats where this simple yet powerfully effective movement comes in.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           How to:
                          </strong>
                          Position the back of your shoulders across a stable bench, feet planted firmly on the ground, about six inches away from your butt (
                          <strong>
                           a
                          </strong>
                          ). Squeezing the glutes, push through your heels to rise up into a bridge position with the hips fully extended. The shoulders down to the knees should be in line, with the knees bent at 90 degrees.Hold the position at the top, glutes, core and hamstrings engaged(
                          <strong>
                           b
                          </strong>
                          ). Lower the hips down and repeat for three sets of eight reps (
                          <strong>
                           c
                          </strong>
                          ). Beginners can continue with just bodyweight, whereas more advanced lifters can progress to rolling a barbell over the top of the hips for added difficulty.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          With all these exercises, pay close attention to form and execution. Continue to add weight to each lift once you can complete two more reps than prescribed with your training weight. Keep it up and after a few workouts youll start to noticerapid gains in strengthand overall fitness. Within a few weeks youll have these exercises mastered and be on your way to having a body that better serves you!
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <em>
                           By Eric Bach for

If you spent half an hour having sex daily, that could lead to a weight loss of 10 pounds or more over the course of a year. Strength Training\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E In addition to burning calories, sex aids in testosterone production, which can strengthen bones and muscles. Testosterone is also responsible for maintaining healthy energy levels, mood, fertility, and sexual desire. So having sex today could help keep your sex drive up down the road. Decreasing testosterone levels, known as andropause or male menopause, can result in a number of side effects including decreased libido, fatigue and depression, among others.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Fdating\u002Flove_tip\u002F59_love_tip.html\"\u003E7 Sexual Positions Women Enjoy \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E3. Cancer Prevention\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E A number of studies show that men who ejaculate on a regular basis are more than 30% less likely to develop&#xA0;prostate cancer. &#xA0;Regular ejaculation, whether from intercourse or masturbation, help flush out the prostate, which may help curb the development of prostate cancer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E4. Improved Cardiovascular Health\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E Because sex is a good form of exercise, it makes sense that it would positively impact the health of your heart. A study from Queens University shows that men who have sex more than three times a week cut their risk of heart attack and stroke in half. Sex has also been shown to lower blood pressure, which further accounts for the overall positive impact on cardiovascular health. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Ftop_10\u002Fdating\u002Fsex-basics.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Sex Basics To Up Your Bedroom Game\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E5. Stress Relief\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E The decreased blood pressure that can result from sex could help lower your stress level. Various study participants have been shown to have a smaller rise in blood pressure during stressful situations after sex, as compared to other test subjects. Moreover, sex releases feel-good endorphins that can help lower anxiety. He referred her to a surgical oncologist, who biopsied the site and had dire news: Jacqueline had skin cancer, a stage IIIC melanoma that had metastasized and was just a whisper shy of slipping into stage IV cancer. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA shocking diagnosis for anyone to handle, Jacqueline was especially incredulous: She was a young African-American woman with no family history of skin cancer, and she had never engaged in behaviors like tanning that studies show correlate with a higher risk.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I was totally shocked by the diagnosis &#x2014; my first thought was, &#x2018;Melanoma is the \u003Ci\u003Edeadly\u003C\u002Fi\u003E skin cancer&#x2019; &#x2014; I never had a reason for it to be on my radar, and never thought I had to prevent it,&#x201D; Jacqueline tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;I had always heard melanoma was a risk for fair-skinned, middle-aged Caucasian women.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F711e45012eb3aba60d4f9bbc1c1665fbdbfcbaca.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJacqueline Smith has survived two melanoma diagnoses. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Jacqueline Smith)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJacqueline, who&#x2019;s now working as the regional assistant for New York Sen. Kirsten Gillibrand, had the cancerous lymph nodes removed when she was just 21 years old. Young age and otherwise good health appeared to be on her side when subsequent scans showed no evidence of cancer, and doctors declared her clear to go on with life. My doctor told me, &#x2018;It will be a miracle if you survive another five years,&#x2019;&#x201D; shares Jacqueline.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe hidden skin cancer risks for people of color&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps even more surprising is that Jacqueline&#x2019;s case isn&#x2019;t an anomaly. While Caucasians are more likely to be diagnosed with skin cancer, only 16 percent of cases involve advanced-stage cancer. In comparison, 52 percent of African-Americans and 26 percent of Hispanic patients are diagnosed with late-stage cases, according to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.skincancer.org\u002Fprevention\u002Fskin-cancer-and-skin-of-color\"\u003ESkin Cancer Foundation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe initial site of Jacqueline&#x2019;s melanoma has never been determined. People of color are more likely to be diagnosed with melanoma in unusual areas like between the toes, under the nails, behind the ears, on the palms of hands and soles of feet, inside the lips, and between the buttock cheeks. Melanoma can even develop in the eyes, the lungs, the gastrointestinal tract, and the membrane known as the meninges that covers the brain and spinal cord.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F3-tips-to-apply-sunscreen-the-right-way-you-know-119381099947.html\"\u003E3 Tips to Apply Sunscreen the Right Way\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;While we know UV light plays a role in melanomas found on Caucasian skin, the primary risk factors for melanoma in people with skin of color has yet to be determined,&#x201D; New York dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.drwhitneybowe.com\"\u003EWhitney Bowe, MD\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;That&#x2019;s why patients with darker skin may get melanomas in areas that we don&#x2019;t commonly associate with sun exposure.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis time around for Jacqueline, driving the cancer back into remission was grueling. She had all of her pelvic lymph nodes removed and underwent Interferon drug treatment and radiation over the course of a year that had her coping with painful open wound burns. While she finally did achieve remission, Jacqueline was left with lymphedema in one leg, a permanent severe swelling that is caused by lymphatic system blockage.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I keep the lymphedema in perspective &#x2014; I have two legs that still work and I have my health, yet it&#x2019;s difficult being young and having so many restrictions. Once upon a time, just being able to choose my shoes was something I took for granted &#x2014; now, I can&#x2019;t fit into most regular shoes,&#x201D; she explains.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELymphedema, which Jacqueline cites as her greatest survivor challenge, is a risk associated with lymph node removal after melanoma and breast cancer surgeries. &#x201C;The risk of developing lymphedema is dependent upon the number of lymph nodes removed &#x2014; so if melanoma is diagnosed early, there may be no lymph node dissection at all, and therefore no risk of lymphedema,&#x201D; says Deborah Lindquist, MD, an oncologist with Arizona Oncology, a practice in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.usoncology.com\"\u003Ethe US Oncology Network\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Lindquist adds that a drug to treat the chronic condition is currently in clinical trials and may be available to the public in the near future.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to the Skin Cancer Foundation, Hispanics account for the highest amount of new skin cancer cases among people of color. &#x201C;Melanoma incidence is increasing rapidly in Latinos, who are outpacing African-Americans likely due to more tanning bed usage,&#x201D; explains New Jersey dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fimagedermatology.com\"\u003EJeanine B. Downie\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, MD. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EExperts recommend wearing sunscreen with an SPF of 30 or higher as the best way to prevent skin cancer and melanoma in people of any color. Jacqueline now follows the advice religiously; she always has sunscreen in her bag (favorites include sprays by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.neutrogena.com\u002Fcategory\u002Fsun\u002Fsunscreen+spray.do\"\u003ENeutrogena\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;such as CoolDry Sport Sunscreen Spray and Ultra Sheer Body Mist Sunscreen), as she finds the spray formulas absorb without the chalkiness of other more traditional formulas. &#x201C;Please don&#x2019;t think you don&#x2019;t need sunscreen because your skin color is natural protectant from the sun &#x2014; anyone with skin is at risk for developing melanoma,&#x201D; she warns. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-scary-causes-behind-the-rise-in-skin-cancer-118288125190.html\"\u003EThe Scary Causes Behind the Rise in Skin Cancer Rates\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost importantly, experts say to get familiar with your skin, so that you notice any changes to new or existing spots and moles. Melanoma is virtually always curable if detected early. &#x201C;If the mole is multicolored, very dark, growing rapidly in size, painful, or stands out as totally different from your other moles, have a dermatologist check it out,&#x201D; Downie says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHave an annual skin checkup with your dermatologist to assess new and old spots, and if you&#x2019;ve previously had precancerous or cancerous lesions, you should go even more regularly &#x2014; every six months. When visiting other doctors like your ophthalmologist and gynecologist, have them check for any unusual signs that you can&#x2019;t see, and ask the same of your hair stylist, who experts say is often your first line of defense against skin cancer on the scalp. &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn fact, New York hair stylist Roman Kusayev of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fromanksalon.com\"\u003ERoman K Salon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E recently detected a melanoma on a regular Latina client&#x2019;s scalp while applying hair color. &#x201C;I noticed a suspicious slightly red spot on her scalp that clearly wasn&#x2019;t a wound or scab. I didn&#x2019;t want to scare her, but I knew I had the responsibility to bring it to her attention,&#x201D; Kusayev tells Yahoo Health. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe client soon made an appointment with her dermatologist, who diagnosed the lesion as skin cancer. Fortunately, the early detection made for routine removal. Hairstyles like tightly parted ponytails and tight braids can leave the scalp vulnerable to the sun&#x2019;s UV rays. Experts recommend wearing a hat or brushing hair back when out in the sun so as not to harshly part and expose swaths of scalp to UV rays. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you do see something pop up that gives you a funny feeling, Jacqueline says to always trust your instinct. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s important to be your own health advocate. I didn&#x2019;t stop harassing doctors until I definitively found out what was wrong, and that is what saved my life.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-part-of-your-face-you-absolutely-need-to-122973275813.html\"\u003EThe Part of Your Face You Absolutely Need to Protect From the Sun \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Goblet Squat\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESquats are an exercise many people struggle to perform safely and effectively. Luckily,&#xA0;the goblet squat&#xA0;is a great progression from a bodyweight squat before squatting with a bar. Because the load is held in front, the core works double-time to keep you tall, while your legs work to control your movement down and stand back up.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdailyburn.com\u002Flife\u002Ffitness\u002Fmental-trick-maintain-strength\u002F?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises\"\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe 5-Second Mental Trick That Could Help You Maintain Strength\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EHold a dumbbell with both hands underneath the &#x201C;bell&#x201D; at chest level, and set your feet shoulder-width apart with your toes pointing slightly outwards (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Push your butt back like you&#x2019;re sitting in a chair and descend until your elbows reach the inside of your knees. (\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Keeping your heels flat, pressing jnto the floor, pause at the bottom of the squat, and return to a full standing position. If your heels rise push your hips further back and work on partial ranges of motion until mobility and form improve (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Repeat for four sets of 8-10 reps.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdailyburn.com\u002Flife\u002Frecipes\u002Fprotein-smoothie-recipes\u002F?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises\"\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E7 Delicious Protein Smoothie Recipes\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cimg alt=\"Pallof Press\" height=\"225\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002F7bd83a76cdc27e2970d546081bc1f0f1b97d9510.gif\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(GIF:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=bzE553my1o8&amp;feature=youtu.be\"\u003ETony Gentilcore\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Ch3\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E2. Pallof Press\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Pallof press is one of those movements that looks confusing, but is actually incredibly simple and beneficial, says Mike Campbell, personal trainer and owner of&#xA0;Unleash Your Alpha. While you may not be hoisting heavy weight, the real challenge lies in&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003Eresisting&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fem\u003Emovement &#x2014; in this case, rotation. That makes this an &#x2018;anti-rotation&#x2019; movement, forcing you to engage through your entire core: obliques, abs, lower back, glutes and more. According to Campbell, the Paloff press will build great usable strength while adding athletic definition through the mid-section (in coordination with a sound diet).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdailyburn.com\u002Flife\u002Ffitness\u002Fbeginner-crossfit-workouts\u002F?partner=yahoo&amp;mtype=5&amp;sub_id=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=yahoo&amp;utm_campaign=01142015_beststrengthexercises&amp;utm_content=01142015_beststrengthexercises\"\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E5 Beginner-Friendly CrossFit Workouts\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E&#xA0;Stand perpendicular to a cable column with the column&#x2019;s arm set around shoulder height. Grab the handle with both hands and pull it in to the chest, maintaining tension on the cable. Feet should be shoulder-width apart, and the feet, knees, hips and shoulders all remain square and facing straight ahead throughout movement (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Holding the chest high, squeeze through the stomach and press the handle away from the body, extending the arms straight while resisting any twisting or rotation (\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). It&#x2019;s at this point the resistance will be highest. Continue to engage your core, and ensure you remain square and straight and resist the rotational force. Bring arms back in to the chest and repeat for three sets of 10 reps per side (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcdn3.dailyburn.com\u002Flife\u002Fwp-content\u002Fuploads\u002F2014\u002F10\u002FOne-Arm-Dumbbell-Row.gif\"\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"One Arm Dumbbell Row\" height=\"226\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002Fc663f42acc7cfc46fcec7daca4e6bede83b7a995.gif\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(GIF:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=ovTHP1MZbZI\"\u003Einfosport\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Ch3\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E3. Dumbbell Row\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMost of us spend more time training the &#x201C;mirror muscles&#x201D; on the front of the body, and neglect what we can&#x2019;t see, according to Campbell. But developing a strong back is key to balance things out, improve posture and&#xA0;avoid injury. The dumbbell row can help achieve all that, in addition building strong arms and a strong core. The main muscles being used are the lats, traps and rhomboids, which reinforce good posture by pulling your shoulders back and aiding the core in stabilizing your spine.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EGrab a dumbbell (20 pounds is plenty for most to start) and find a bench. Start with your left hand on the bench with left arm extended, while your right arm holds the dumbbell and right foot is on the ground (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Retract your shoulders, brace your abs, and pull the weight up on the side of your body until the elbow passes the side of the body (\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Lower under control and repeat for three sets of 6-8 reps on each side (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cimg alt=\"Push Up\" height=\"225\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002F0538bd62f3d9280916e85bfcdb0426558175e612.gif\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(GIF:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdailyburn.com\u002Flife\u002Ffitness\u002Fperfect-push-up-workout-video\u002F\"\u003EDailyBurn\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Ch3\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E4. Push-Up\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe&#xA0;push-up&#xA0;might appear basic, but it&#x2019;s one of the best exercises you can do. The functional movement is great for training the upper-body pushing muscles &#x2014; the anterior deltoids, triceps and chest. It also requires you to engage your core and allows full range of motion in your shoulder blades, unlike the bench press.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EStart on your knees facing the floor with your hands at shoulder-width, planted directly under the shoulders. Assume a plank position by straightening your legs, supporting your weight with hands and feet (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Squeeze your backside to keep your trunk engaged and lower your body slowly to the ground. The elbows should be slightly tucked &#x2014; like arrows, rather than flared like the letter &#x201C;T&#x201D; (\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Descend until your chest is just above the ground and return to the starting position by fully extending your arms, and repeat (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Note: If you can&#x2019;t do five push-ups with good form, elevate your hands on a bench or chair to begin building up your strength. If push-ups are easy,&#xA0;try elevating your feet&#xA0;on a chair on adding a weight vest. Make sure you&#x2019;re able to perform three sets of 12 push-ups with your bodyweight before adding a vest or elevating your feet.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cimg alt=\"Split Squat\" height=\"225\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002Fa42dad071727e39d308f306e4d4f01eec462a44a.gif\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(GIF:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=z0NUTXY1vF0\"\u003EHowcast Sports Fitness\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Ch3\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E5. Split Squat\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETraditional squats are great, but it&#x2019;s important to incorporate single-leg movements to develop athleticism and&#xA0;minimize training imbalances. The split squat, a stationary lunge, does just that. The split stance requires you to balance with a narrow base of support, firing up stabilizing muscles of the hip and trunk while training your quads, glutes and hamstrings to perform the movement. In addition to building&#xA0;lower-body strength, the single-leg nature of the exercise helps improve balance and increase flexibility and stability in the hips.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EStand with feet shoulder-width apart. Next, take a step forward with your right foot, and a large step backwards with your left foot &#x2014; this is your starting position (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Keep the front heel flat and descend into a lunge, bringing your back knee towards the floor. Stop just short of the knee touching the ground on the back leg with the front heel still flat on the ground (\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Pause for one second and return to standing. Perform 6-8 reps on your right leg, then 6-8 reps on your left leg, and repeat for three sets (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cimg alt=\"Lateral Squat\" height=\"225\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002F8d997ede9fb5f45fdbc1e29b8dc9a14a2d0832f1.gif\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(GIF:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.coreperformance.com\u002Fknowledge\u002Fmovements\u002Flateral-squat.html\"\u003ECore Performance\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E6. Lateral Squat\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe lateral squat combines two movements: a lateral lunge and a squat. The difference? The lateral squat is stationary. It requires you to move side-to-side, providing a great stretch on the groin and inner thighs while training the hips, thighs and trunk to work together. Life isn&#x2019;t strictly moving forwards and backwards. It&#x2019;s best that your training isn&#x2019;t either.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EStand tall with your feet wider than shoulder-width apart, heels flat on the ground and toes pointed forward. Initiate the movement by pushing your hips backwards, bending your left leg, and leaning to your left with your right foot angled out slightly (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). The left knee should be bent, left heel flat on the floor, and right leg extended with your weight over the left side of your body (\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). This is one rep. Return to a standing position and descend doing the same movement on your right side to even things out (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Perform six reps per leg for three sets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cdiv\u003E\n \u003Cimg alt=\"Glute Bridge\" height=\"225\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002F27addc7a070f8297a75bd3765f24d4c73a499278.gif\"\u003E\n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(GIF:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=SEdqd1n0cvg\"\u003EScott Herman Fitness\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Ch3\u003E7\u003Cstrong\u003E. Hip Extension (Glute Bridges\u002FHip Thrusts)\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne of the most important muscle groups for any trainee &#x2014; athlete, weekend warrior, or newbie &#x2014; is the glutes. Yet they are often neglected and underutilized from sitting for long periods each day. According to Campbell, &#x201C;When we attempt movements from running to squatting without optimal hip movement we risk injury to our hips, knees and ankles. Getting glutes that not only switch on when they should but are strong is crucial, and that&#x2019;s where this simple yet powerfully effective movement comes in.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHow to:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E&#xA0;Position the back of your shoulders across a stable bench, feet planted firmly on the ground, about six inches away from your butt (\u003Cstrong\u003Ea\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Squeezing the glutes, push through your heels to rise up into a bridge position with the hips fully extended. The shoulders down to the knees should be in line, with the knees bent at 90 degrees.&#xA0;Hold the position at the top, glutes, core and hamstrings engaged&#xA0;(\u003Cstrong\u003Eb\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Lower the hips down and repeat for three sets of eight reps (\u003Cstrong\u003Ec\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E). Beginners can continue with just bodyweight, whereas more advanced lifters can progress to rolling a barbell over the top of the hips for added difficulty.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWith all these exercises, pay close attention to form and execution. Continue to add weight to each lift once you can complete two more reps than prescribed with your training weight. Keep it up and after a few workouts you&#x2019;ll start to notice&#xA0;rapid gains in strength&#xA0;and overall fitness. Within a few weeks you&#x2019;ll have these exercises mastered and be on your way to having a body that better serves you!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EBy Eric Bach for&#xA0;\u003Ca
